NEW ISSUES ‑ BOOK‑ENTRY ONLY RATINGS: See "RATINGS" herein
In the opinion of co-bond counsel, assuming compliance by the City with certain covenants, under existing statutes, regulations, and judicial 
decisions, the interest on the Series 2024 Bonds will be excluded from gross income for federal income tax purposes of the holders thereof and will 
not be an item of tax preference for purposes of the federal alternative minimum tax; however, interest on the Series 2024 Bonds may be included 
in the "adjusted financial statement income" of certain "applicable corporations" that are subject to the 15-percent alternative minimum tax under 
section 55 of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as amended.  See "TAX MATTERS" herein for a description of other tax consequences to holders of the 
Series 2024 Bonds.

This 
Official Statement relates to the issuance and sale by the City of Orlando, Florida (the "City") of $132,605,000 in aggregate principal amount 
of its Water Reclamation System Improvement Revenue Bonds, Series 2024A (the "Series 2024A Bonds") and $17,120,000 in aggregate principal amount 
of its Water Reclamation System Refunding Revenue Bonds, Series 2024B (the "Series 2024B Bonds" and, together with the Series 2024A Bonds, the 
"Series 2024 Bonds") pursuant to, among other things, that certain Master Wastewater System Bond Ordinance enacted by the City Council of the City 
(the "City Council") on December 3, 2012, as previously supplemented (the "Master Bond Ordinance"), and particularly as supplemented by that certain 
resolution adopted by the City Council on September 23, 2024 bearing documentary number 240923B08 (the "Series 2024 Resolution" and, together with 
the Master Bond Ordinance, the "Bond Ordinance").  All capitalized terms used herein and not otherwise expressly defined herein shall have the meanings 
set forth in "APPENDIX B – THE BOND ORDINANCE" attached hereto.
The proceeds of the Series 2024A Bonds will be used for the purpose of financing, together with other legally available funds of the City, (a) all or a 
portion of the costs of the 2024 Project (as defined herein); (b) a deposit to the Composite Reserve Account in the amount of the Reserve Requirement (as 
defined herein) allocable to the Series 2024A Bonds; and (c) the costs of issuance in connection with the Series 2024A Bonds.  See "PLAN OF FINANCE" 
and "ESTIMATED SOURCES AND USES OF FUNDS" herein and "APPENDIX A  –  CONSULTING ENGINEER'S REPORT  –  5.0 Capital Improvement 
Projects" attached hereto.
The proceeds of the Series 2024B Bonds will be used for the purpose of financing, together with other legally available funds of the City, (a) the cost 
of the refunding and redemption of the Refunded Bonds (as defined herein); (b) a deposit to the Composite Reserve Account in the amount of the Reserve 
Requirement allocable to the Series 2024B Bonds; and (c) the costs of issuance in connection with the Series 2024B Bonds.  See "PLAN OF FINANCE" and 
"ESTIMATED SOURCES AND USES OF FUNDS" herein.
The Series 2024 Bonds will be issued as fully registered bonds, without coupons, in denominations of $5,000 or any integral multiple thereof, and 
initially will be registered in the name of Cede & Co., as nominee of The Depository Trust Company ("DTC").  Purchases of beneficial ownership interests 
in the Series 2024 Bonds will be made in book‑entry form only, and purchasers will not receive physical delivery of bond certificates representing the 
beneficial ownership interests in the Series 2024 Bonds so purchased.  Payments of principal of, premium, if any, and interest on, any Series 2024 Bond 
will be made to Cede & Co., as nominee for DTC, as registered owner of the Series 2024 Bonds, by Computershare Trust Company, N.A., as successor to 
Wells Fargo Bank, National Association, as registrar and paying agent, to be subsequently disbursed to the Beneficial Owners (as defined in APPENDIX E 
attached hereto) of the Series 2024 Bonds.  See "APPENDIX E – DTC AND THE BOOK‑ENTRY ONLY SYSTEM" attached hereto.
Interest on the Series 2024 Bonds is payable semiannually on April 1 and October 1 of each year, commencing on April 1, 2025.  The Series 2024 Bonds 
will bear interest at the rates and will be payable as to principal in the amounts and on the dates set forth on the inside front cover page of this Official 
Statement.  See "DESCRIPTION OF THE SERIES 2024 BONDS – General" herein.
Certain of the Series 2024A Bonds may be subject to redemption prior to maturity as more fully described under the caption "DESCRIPTION OF THE 
SERIES 2024 BONDS – Redemption Provisions" herein.  The Series 2024B Bonds are not subject to optional redemption prior to their maturity.
The Series 2024 Bonds are special limited obligations of the City payable from and secured by a pledge of the Pledged Revenues, which primarily 
consist of the Net Revenues derived by the City from the operation of the Water Reclamation System (as defined herein) and the Pledged Utilities 
Services Tax in the manner and to the extent provided in the Bond Ordinance, all on a parity with the lien of any Parity Contract Obligations and any 
Additional Parity Obligations issued under the Bond Ordinance.  See "SECURITY AND SOURCES OF PAYMENT FOR THE SERIES 2024 BONDS" herein 
and "APPENDIX B – THE BOND ORDINANCE" attached hereto.
THE SERIES 2024 BONDS DO NOT CONSTITUTE A GENERAL OBLIGATION OR INDEBTEDNESS OF THE CITY WITHIN THE 
MEANING OF ANY CONSTITUTIONAL, STATUTORY OR CHARTER PROVISIONS OR LIMITATIONS, BUT WILL BE PAYABLE SOLELY 
FROM AND SECURED BY A LIEN UPON AND A PLEDGE OF THE PLEDGED REVENUES IN THE MANNER AND TO THE EXTENT 
PROVIDED IN THE BOND ORDINANCE.  NO HOLDER OF SERIES 2024 BONDS SHALL EVER HAVE THE RIGHT TO COMPEL THE 
EXERCISE OF THE AD VALOREM TAXING POWER OF THE CITY OR TAXATION IN ANY FORM ON ANY REAL OR PERSONAL 
PROPERTY, OR TO COMPEL THE CITY TO PAY SUCH PRINCIPAL AND INTEREST ON THE SERIES 2024 BONDS FROM ANY OTHER 
FUNDS OF THE CITY.  THE SERIES 2024 BONDS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE A LIEN UPON THE WATER RECLAMATION SYSTEM, 
OR ANY PART THEREOF, OR ON ANY OTHER PROPERTY OF OR IN THE CITY, BUT SHALL CONSTITUTE A LIEN ONLY ON THE 
PLEDGED REVENUES IN THE MANNER AND TO THE EXTENT PROVIDED IN THE BOND ORDINANCE.
This cover page contains certain limited information for quick reference only.  It is not, and is not intended to be, a summary of the matters relating 
to the Series 2024 Bonds.  Potential investors should read the entire Official Statement, including the inside front cover page and the appendices attached 
hereto, to obtain information essential to the making of an informed investment decision.
The Series 2024 Bonds will be offered when, as, and if issued by the City and received by the below referenced underwriters, subject to prior sale 
and to withdrawal or modification of the offer without notice, and subject to the approving opinions of Bryant Miller Olive P.A., Orlando, Florida, 
and Marcelo Llorente, P.A., Miami, Florida, in their capacity as co
-
bond counsel.  Certain legal matters will be passed upon for the City by Greenberg 
Traurig, P.A. and Charles Hawkins II, P.A., both of Orlando, Florida, in their capacity as co-disclosure counsel.  Certain other legal matters will be 
passed upon for the City by Endow Law P.A., Orlando, Florida, in its capacity as special legal counsel.  Certain legal matters will be passed upon 
for the underwriters by its counsel, Marchena and Graham, P.A., Orlando, Florida.  PFM Financial Advisors LLC, Orlando, Florida, is serving as 
financial advisor to the City.  The Series 2024 Bonds are expected to be delivered through the book
-
entry system of DTC on or about October 30, 2024.

INTRODUCTION 
General 
The purpose of this Official Statement, which includes the inside front cover page and the 
appendices attached hereto, is to provide certain information in connection with the issuance and 
sale by the City of Orlando, Florida (the "City") of $132,605,000 in aggregate principal amount of 
its Water Reclamation System Improvement Revenue Bonds, Seri es 2024A (the "Series 2024A 
Bonds") and $17,120,000 in aggregate principal am ount of its Water R eclamation System 
Refunding Revenue Bonds, Series 2024B (the "Series 2024B Bonds" and, together with the Series 
2024A Bonds, the "Series 2024 Bonds") .  All capitalized terms used  herein and not otherwise 
expressly defined herein shall have the m eanings set forth in "APPENDIX B – THE BOND 
ORDINANCE" attached hereto. 
This Introduction is not a summary of this Official Statement and is intended only for quick 
reference.  It is only a brief description of and guide to, and is qualified in its entirety by reference 
to, the more complete and detailed informati on contained in the entir e Official Statement, 
including the inside front cover page and the appendices attached hereto, and the documents 
summarized or described herein.  A full review should be made of  the entire Official Statement, 
including the inside front cover  page and the appendices attached  hereto, and of the documents 
summarized or described herein.  The offering of  the Series 2024 Bonds to potential investors is 
made only by means of the entire Official Statement.  No person is authorized to detach this 
Introduction from this O fficial Statement or to otherwise use it without the entire Official 
Statement, including the inside front cover page and the appendices attached hereto. 
Authorization for the Series 2024 Bonds 
The Series 2024 Bonds will be issued pursuant to: (a) the Constitution and laws of the State 
of Florida (the "State"), particularly Article VI II, Section 2, Constitution of the State of Florida, 
Chapter 166, Part II and Section 159.11, Florida Statutes, as amended; (b) the City's Home Rule 
Ordinance bearing documentary number 17943 enacted by the City Council of the City (the "City 
Council") on July 25, 1983; and (c) that certain  Master Wastewater System Bond Ordinance No. 
2012-53 enacted by the City Counc il on December 3, 2012, as previously supplemented (the 
"Master Bond Ordinance"), and particularly as supplemented by that certain resolution adopted by 
the City Council on September 23, 2024 bearing documentary number 240923B08 (the "Series  
2 
2024 Resolution" and, together wi th the Master Bond Ordinance, the "Bond Ordinance").  See 
"APPENDIX B – THE BOND ORDINANCE" attached hereto. 
Purpose of the Series 2024 Bonds 
The proceeds of the Series 2024A Bonds will be used for the purpose of financing, together 
with other legally available funds of the City, (a) all or  a portion of the cost s of the 2024 Project 
(as defined herein); (b) a deposit to the Composite Reserve Account in the amount of the Reserve 
Requirement (as defined herein) allocable to the Series 2024A Bonds; and (c) the costs of issuance 
in connection with th e Series 2024A Bonds.  See "PLAN OF FINANCE" and "ESTIMATED 
SOURCES AND USES OF FUNDS" herein and "APPENDIX A – CONSULTING ENGINEER'S 
REPORT – 5.0 Capital Improvement Projects" attached hereto. 
The proceeds of the Series 2024B Bonds will be used for the purpose of financing, together 
with other legally available funds of the City, (a) the cost of the refunding and redemption of the 
Refunded Bonds (as defined herein); (b) a deposit to the Composite Reserve Account in the amount 
of the Reserve Requirement allocable to the Series 2024B Bonds; and (c) the costs of issuance in 
connection with the Series 2024B Bonds.  See "PLAN OF FINANCE" and "ESTIMATED 
SOURCES AND USES OF FUNDS" herein. 
Description of the Series 2024 Bonds 
The Series 2024 Bonds will be issued as fully registered bonds, without coupons, in 
denominations of $5,000 or any integral multiple th ereof, and initially will be registered in the 
name of Cede & Co., as nominee of The Depos itory Trust Company ("DTC").  Purchases of 
beneficial ownership interests in the Series 2024 Bonds will be made in book-entry form only, and 
purchasers will not receive physic al delivery of bond certificates representing the beneficial 
ownership interests in the Series 2024 Bonds so purchased.  Payments of principal of, premium, if 
any, and interest on, any Series 2024 Bond will be made to Cede & Co., as nominee for DTC, as 
registered owner of the Series 2024 Bonds, by Computershare Trust Company, N.A., as successor 
to Wells Fargo Bank, National Associ ation, as registrar (the "Regis trar") and paying agent (the 
"Paying Agent"), to be subsequently disbur sed to the Beneficial Owners (as defined in 
APPENDIX E attached hereto) of the Series 2024 Bonds.  See "APPENDIX E – DTC AND THE 
BOOK-ENTRY ONLY SYSTEM" attached hereto. 
Interest on the Series 2024 Bonds is paya ble semiannually on April 1 and October 1 of 
each year, commencing on April 1, 2025.  The Series 2024 Bonds will bear interest at the rates 
and will be payable as to principal in the amoun ts and on the dates set forth on the inside front 
cover page of this Official Statement.   See "DESCRIPTION OF THE SERIES 2024 
BONDS – General" herein. 
Certain of the Series 2024A Bonds may be subject to redemption prior to maturity as more 
fully described under the caption "DESCRIPTION OF THE SERIES 2024 BONDS – Redemption 
Provisions" herein.  The Series 2024B Bonds are not subject to redemption prior to their maturity.

Security and Sources of Payment for the Series 2024 Bonds 
The Series 2024 Bonds are special limited obligations of the City payable from and secured 
by a pledge of the Pledged Revenues, which primarily consist of the Net Revenues derived by the 
City from the operation of the Water Reclamati on System (as defined he rein) and the Pledged 
Utilities Services Tax in the manner and to the extent provided in the Bond Ordinance, all on a 
parity with the lien of any Parity Contract Obligations and any Additional Parity Obligations issued 
under the Bond Ordinance.  See "SECUR ITY AND SOURCES OF PAYMENT FOR THE 
SERIES 2024 BONDS" herein and "APPEND IX B – THE BOND ORDINANCE" attached 
hereto. 
THE SERIES 2024 BONDS DO NOT CONSTITUTE A GENERAL OBLIGATION 
OR INDEBTEDNESS OF THE CITY  WITHIN THE MEANING OF ANY 
CONSTITUTIONAL, STATUTORY OR CHART ER PROVISIONS OR LIMITATIONS, 
BUT WILL BE PAYABLE SOLELY FROM AND SECURED BY A LIEN UPON AND A 
PLEDGE OF THE PLEDGED REVENUES IN THE MANNER AND TO THE EXTENT 
PROVIDED IN THE BOND ORDINANCE.  NO HOLDER OF SERIES 2024 BONDS 
SHALL EVER HAVE THE RIGHT TO COMPEL THE EXERCI SE OF THE AD 
VALOREM TAXING POWER OF THE CITY OR TAXATION IN ANY FORM ON ANY 
REAL OR PERSONAL PROPERTY, OR TO COMPEL THE CITY  TO PAY SUCH 
PRINCIPAL AND INTEREST ON THE SERIES 2024 BONDS FROM ANY OTHER 
FUNDS OF THE CITY.  THE SERIES 2024 BONDS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE A LIEN 
UPON THE WATER RECLAMATION SYSTEM, OR ANY PART THEREOF, OR ON 
ANY OTHER PROPERTY OF OR IN THE CITY, BUT SHALL CONSTITUTE A LIEN 
ONLY ON THE PLEDGED REVENUES IN THE MANNER AND TO THE EXTENT 
PROVIDED IN THE BOND ORDINANCE. 
The City 
The City was incorporated on July 31, 1875 and is centrally loca ted in the State, 
approximately 150 miles south of the Florida-Georgia state line, 50  miles west of the Atlantic 
Ocean and 75 miles east of the Gulf of Mexico.  See "THE CITY" herein. 
The Water Reclamation System 
References to the "Water Reclamation Syst em" herein shall have the same meaning 
assigned to the term "System" in the B ond Ordinance.  See "APPENDIX B – THE BOND 
ORDINANCE" attached hereto. 
The Water Reclamation System is operated by the Water Reclamation Division within the 
City's Department of Public Works.  The Water  Reclamation System is an integrated system 
comprised of: (a) a collection system to collect and transmit wastewater from customers to the 
water reclamation facilities for treatment; (b) th ree WRFs (as defined he rein), including (i) the 
Iron Bridge Plant (as defined here in), (ii) the Conserv I Plant (a s defined herein), and (iii) the 
Conserv II Plant (as defined herein), which treat the incoming wastewater to a point where it is 
safe to be reused in the community for irrigation and other beneficial purposes; and (c) a reclaimed 
water distribution system to convey the treated wa ter to irrigation customer s to use in lieu of  
4 
drinking water, to rapid infiltra tion basins for aquifer recharge or to environmental enhancement 
projects such as man-made wetlands systems.  Together, these components provide a 
comprehensive means of collecting, treating, and beneficially reusing wastewater for the City.  See 
"THE WATER RECLAMATION SYSTEM," "WATER RECLAMATION SYSTEM FINANCE 
MATTERS" and "FINANCIAL STATEMENTS" herein. 
Consulting Engineer's Report 
In support of the City's planned issuance of the Series 2024 Bonds, the City authorized the 
Consulting Engineer (as defined herein) to prep are the Consulting Engineer's Report (as defined 
herein).  See "CONSULTING E NGINEER'S REPORT" herein and 
"APPENDIX A – CONSULTING ENGINEER'S REPORT" attached hereto.

of Rule 15c2-12 of the U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission (the "SEC") promulgated 
pursuant to the Securities Exchange Act of 1934 (t he "Exchange Act"), as in effect on the date 
hereof ("Rule 15c2-12"), simultaneously with the issuance of the Series 2024 Bonds, the City, as 
an "obligated person" under Rule 15c2-12, will enter into a Continuing Disclosure Agreement (the 
"Continuing Disclosure Agreemen t") with Digital Assu rance Certification, L.L.C., as initial 
disclosure dissemination agen t ("DAC"), under which the City will undertake to provide 
continuing disclosure with resp ect to the Series 2024 Bonds a nd the Water Reclamation System 
for the benefit of the holder s of the Series 2024 Bonds.  See "CONTINUING DISCLOSURE" 
herein and "APPENDIX D  – FORM OF CONTINUING DI SCLOSURE AGREEMENT" 
attached hereto.

PLAN OF FINANCE 
General 
The proceeds of the Series 2024A Bonds will be used for the purpose of financing, together 
with other legally available funds of the City, (a) all or a portion of the costs of the 2024 Project; 
(b) a deposit to the Composite Reserve Account in the amount of the Reserve Requirement 
allocable to the Series 2024A Bonds; and (c) the costs of issuance in connection with the Series 
2024A Bonds.  See "ESTIMATED SOURCES AND USES OF FUNDS" herein and "APPENDIX 
A – CONSULTING ENGINEER'S REPORT – 5.0 Capital Improvement Projects" attached 
hereto. 
The proceeds of the Series 2024B Bonds will be used for the purpose of financing, together 
with other legally available funds of the City, (a) the cost of the refunding and redemption of the 
Refunded Bonds; (b) a deposit to the Composite Reserve Account in the amount of the Reserve 
Requirement allocable to the Series 2024B Bonds; and (c) the costs of issuance in connection with 
the Series 2024B Bonds.  See "ESTIMATED SOURCES AND USES OF FUNDS" herein. 
The 2024 Project 
A portion of the proceeds of the Series 2024A Bonds will be used to finance all or a portion 
of the "2024 Project," which includes the acquisition, construction and equipping of replacements 
and improvements to the Water Recl amation System as more particularly described in the Series 
2024 Resolution, together with such other re placements and improve ments to the Water 
Reclamation System as shall be authorized and approved by the City through its budgetary control 
processes.  For additional information regarding the capital improvement projects composing the 
2024 Project, which are expected to be funded with a portion of the proceeds of the Series 2024A 
Bonds, see "APPENDIX A – CONSULTING ENGINEER'S REPORT – 5.0 Capital Improvement 
Projects" attached hereto.  The allocation of the proceeds of the Series 2024A Bonds to such capital 
improvement projects may be changed subject to, among other things, approval of the City through 
its budgetary control processes.  See "ESTIMATED SOURCES AND USES OF FUNDS" herein. 
Refunded Bonds 
The City has determined that it is desirable to provide for the refunding and redemption of 
all of the City's Outstanding Wastewater Syst em Refunding and Impr ovement Revenue Bonds, 
Series 2013 (the "Refunded Bonds").  A portion of the proceeds of the Series 2024B Bonds, 
together with other legally available funds of the City, will be deposited with the Paying Agent in 
an amount sufficient to redeem the Refunded Bonds on or about the date of issuance of the Series 
2024B Bonds.  Such other legally available funds will include funds transferred from certain funds 
and accounts held for the benefit of the Re funded Bonds under the Bond Ordinance.  See 
"ESTIMATED SOURCES AND USES OF FUNDS" herein.

DESCRIPTION OF THE SERIES 2024 BONDS 
General 
The Series 2024 Bonds will be dated the date of  their issuance and delivery and will bear 
interest from the dated date thereof at the rates se t forth on the inside front cover page of this 
Official Statement, payable semiannually on April 1 and October 1 of each year, commencing on 
April 1, 2025. 
The Series 2024 Bonds will be issued as fully registered bonds, without coupons, in 
denominations of $5,000 or any integral multiple th ereof, and initially will be registered in the 
name of Cede & Co., as nominee of The Depos itory Trust Company ("DTC").  Purchases of 
beneficial ownership interests in the Series 2024 Bonds will be made in book-entry form only, and 
purchasers will not receive physic al delivery of bond certificates representing the beneficial 
ownership interests in the Series 2024 Bonds so purchased.  Payments of principal of, premium, if 
any, and interest on, any Series 2024 Bond will be made to Cede & Co., as nominee for DTC, as 
registered owner of the Series 2024 Bonds, by the Paying Agent, to be subsequently disbursed to 
the Beneficial Owners (as define d in APPENDIX E attached here to) of the Series 2024 Bonds.  
See "APPENDIX E – DTC AND THE BOOK-ENTRY ONLY SYSTEM" attached hereto. 
Redemption Provisions 
Optional Redemption.  The Series 2024A Bonds maturing prior to October 1, 2035 are not 
subject to optional redemption prior to their maturity.  The Se ries 2024A Bonds maturing on or 
after October 1, 2035 are subject to optional redemption prior to maturity, at the option of the City, 
on any date on or after October 1, 2034, either in whole or in part, at a redemption price of 100% 
of the principal amount of  the Series 2024A Bonds being redeem ed, plus accrued interest to the 
Redemption Date. 
The Series 2024B Bonds are not subject to optional redemption prior to their maturity. 
Mandatory Sinking Fund Redemption .  Each of the Series 20 24A Bonds that are term 
bonds are referred to herein as a "Series 2024A  Term Bond."  The Se ries 2024A Term Bond 
maturing on October 1, 2049 is subject to mandatory redemption prior to maturity by

Notice of Redemption 
Notice of redemption shall, at least 20 days prior to the Redemption Date, be filed with the 
Registrar, and mailed by the Registrar on behalf of the City, first class mail, postage prepaid, to all 
Holders of Series 2024A Bonds to be redeemed at their addresses as they appear on the registration 
books of the City, but failure to mail such notice to one or more Holders of such Series 2024A 
Bonds, or any defect therein, shall not affect th e validity of the proceedings for such redemption 
with respect to Holders of Series 2024A Bonds to which notice was duly mailed and no defect 
occurred.  Each such notice sha ll set forth the date fixed for re demption, the redemption price to 
be paid and, if less than all of such Series 2024A Bonds of one maturity are to  be called, the 
distinctive numbers of such Series 2024A Bonds to be redeemed and, in the case of Series 2024A 
Bonds to be redeemed in part only, the portion of the principal amount thereof to be redeemed. 
Any notice of optional redemp tion may state that redemptio n is conditioned upon receipt 
by the Paying Agent of moneys sufficient to pay the redemption price, plus interest accrued to the 
Redemption Date, or upon the satisfaction of any othe r condition stated in such notice, or that it 
may be rescinded upon the occurrence of any other event, and any conditional notice so given may 
be rescinded at any time before payment of such redemption price and accrued interest if any such 
condition so specified is not satisfied or if any such other event occurs.  Notice of such rescission 
shall be given by the Registrar to affected Holders of such Seri es 2024A Bonds as promptly as 
practicable upon the failure of such condition or the occurrence of such other event. 
Registration, Transfer and Exchange 
If the book-entry only system is discontinued,  the Beneficial Owners (as defined herein) 
shall receive certificated Series 2024 Bonds which will be subj ect to registration of transfer or 
exchange as set forth below.  Transfer of any Series 2024 Bond may be registered upon the 
registration books maintained by the Registrar upon surrender of  such Series 2024 Bond to the 
Registrar together with a proper written instrument  of transfer in form and with guarantee of 
signature satisfactory to the Regi strar.  Upon surrender to the Regi strar, a new fully registered 
Series 2024 Bond of the same Series and ma turity, and of author ized denomination or 
denominations, in the same aggregate principal amount and bearing the same rate of interest will  
9 
be issued to and in the name of the transferee.  The City and the Registrar may charge the registered 
owners of the Series 2024 Bonds an amount sufficient to reimburse them for any tax, fee or other 
governmental charge required to be paid, except for any such governmental charge imposed by the 
City, with respect to the registration of such transfer before any such certificated Series 2024 Bonds 
are delivered.  Neither the City no r the Registrar shall be required to  register the transfer of any 
Series 2024 Bond during the period commencing on the 15th day of the month next preceding an 
interest payment date on the Series 2024 Bonds a nd ending on such interest payment date, or, in 
the case of any proposed redemption of Series 2024 Bonds, after such Series 2024 Bonds or any 
portion thereof have been selected for redemption. 
The City, the Registrar and the Paying Agent shall deem and treat the registered owner of 
any Series 2024 Bond as the absolute owner of such Series 2024 Bond for all purposes, including 
for the purpose of receiving payment of the principal, redemption price, and interest on the Series 
2024 Bonds. 
BOOK-ENTRY ONLY SYSTEM 
Purchases of beneficial ownership interests in the Series 2024 Bonds will be made in 
book-entry form only, and purchas ers will not receive physical  delivery of bond  certificates 
representing the beneficial ow nership interests in the Series  2024 Bonds so purchased.  For a 
description of DTC and the book-entry on ly system, see "APPENDIX E – DTC AND THE 
BOOK-ENTRY ONLY SYSTEM" attached hereto. 
SECURITY AND SOURCES OF PAYMENT FOR THE SERIES 2024 BONDS 
Pledged Revenues 
The Series 2024 Bonds are special limited obligations of the City payable from and secured 
by a pledge of the "Pledged Revenues" consis ting of: (a) the Net Revenues of the Water 
Reclamation System, (b) the Pledged Utilities Serv ices Tax, and (c) until applied in accordance 
with the Bond Ordinance, the moneys on depos it in the various fund s and accounts created 
pursuant to the Bond Ordinance, ex cept (i) as for the Rebate Fund, and (ii) to the extent moneys 
on deposit in an account of the Reserve Fund or th e Project Fund shall be pledged solely for the 
payment of the Series of Bonds for which it was established in accordance with the provisions of 
the Master Bond Ordinance or a Supplemental Ordinance or Resolution, all on a parity with the 
lien of any Parity Contract Obligations and any Additional Parity Obligations issued under the 
Bond Ordinance.  Upon the issuance of the Se ries 2024 Bonds and the refunding and redemption 
of the Refunded Bonds, the Series 2024 Bonds w ill be the only Additional Parity Obligations 
outstanding under the Bond Ordinance.  As of October 1, 2024, there were no Parity Contract 
Obligations outstanding under the Bond Ordinance.  For additional information relating to 
Additional Parity Obligations, including Parity Contract Ob ligations, see "OUTSTANDING 
WATER RECLAMATION SYSTEM OBLIGATIONS – Additional Parity Obligations" herein. 
For information regarding th e Net Revenues, Pledged Util ities Services Tax, Parity 
Contract Obligations, and Additional Parity Obligations, see "SECURITY AND SOURCES OF 
PAYMENT FOR THE SERIES 2024 BONDS – Net Revenues," " – Pledged Utilities Services  
10 
Tax," " – Flow of Funds," " – Additional Pa rity Obligations," and "OUTSTANDING WATER 
RECLAMATION SYSTEM OBLIGATIONS" herein and "APPENDIX B – THE BOND 
ORDINANCE" attached hereto. 
Net Revenues 
"Net Revenues" is defined in the Bond Ordinance as the Gross Revenues or Revenues, after 
deduction of the Cost of Operation and Maintenance. 
"Gross Revenues" or "Revenues" is defined in the Bond Ordinance as all income and 
earnings, including Connection Fees, received by the City or accrued to the City from the 
ownership, use or operation of th e Water Reclamation System and all parts thereof, including, 
without limitation, unencumbered, non-ad valorem special assessments which are not pledged for 
the repayment of, or as security for, any indebt edness of the City, whethe r currently outstanding 
or hereafter issued, other than the Bonds and which are legally available to be used as contemplated 
under the Bond Ordinance, grant m onies received by the City as a result of ownership, use or 
operation of the Water Reclamatio n System that are legally avai lable for the purposes for which 
Gross Revenues or Revenues are applied under the Bond Ordinance, proceeds from the sale or 
other disposition of the Water Reclamation System or any part thereof pursuant to the terms of the 
Bond Ordinance, moneys transferred from the Ra te Stabilization Fund and deposited into the 
Revenue Fund in accordance with the terms of the Bond Ordinance, provided any moneys 
transferred from the Rate Stabilization Fund into the Revenue Fund within 90 days following the 
end of a Fiscal Year may be desi gnated by the City as Gross Revenues of such prior Fiscal Year, 
investment income, if any, earned on any fund or account created pursuant to the Bond Ordinance, 
except the Rebate Fund, all as calculated in accordance with generally accepted accounting 
principles, and any payment received by the C ity from a Qualified Agreement Provider as 
contemplated in the Bond Ordinance; provided, however, that "Gross Revenues" or "Revenues" 
shall not include internal services charges fro m the centralized engin eering group, any direct 
subsidy, rebate or tax credit payment received from the United St ates Treasury with respect to 
Direct Subsidy Obligations, non-ad valorem sp ecial assessments which are pledged for the 
repayment of, or as security for, any indebtedne ss of the City, whether currently outstanding or 
hereafter issued, other than the Bonds, condemna tion awards or proceeds of insurance received 
with respect to the Water Reclam ation System, moneys deposited to the Rate Stabilization Fund 
from the Surplus Fund, including any moneys tran sferred from the Surplus Fund to the Rate 
Stabilization Fund within 90 days following the end of a Fiscal Year whic h the City determines 
not to be Gross Revenues of such prior Fiscal Year, Contributions in Aid of Construction, impact 
fees, or unrealized gains or losses from investments. 
"Cost of Operation and Maintenance" is defined in the Bond Ordinance as the then current 
expenses, paid or accrued, in the operation, ma intenance and repair of  the Water Reclamation 
System, as calculated in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles, including, but 
not limited to, general administra tive and indirect labor costs, personal services, contractual 
services, repairs and maintenance, and materials and supplies, but excluding capital expenditures, 
any reserve for renewals and replacements, a ny allowance for depreciation, any Bond Service 
Requirement, any payments in lieu of taxes, franchise fees or other transfers.  
11 
Pledged Utilities Services Tax 
The principal and interest on Bonds, includ ing the Series 2024 Bonds, are additionally 
payable from and secured equally and ratably by a pledge of and lien upon the Pledged Utilities 
Services Tax, and the City has irrevocably pledge d, in the manner and to the extent provided in 
the Bond Ordinance, the Pledged Utilities Services Tax for the payment of the Costs of Operation 
and Maintenance and the payment of the principal of, premium,  if any, and interest on any 
Additional Parity Obligations and for the funding of the Reserve Fund.  The pledge of and lien 
on the Pledged Utilities Serv ices Tax under the Bond Ordinan ce is junior and subordinate 
in all respects to any pledge thereof and lien thereon with respect to any Senior Lien Utilities 
Services Tax Obligations incurred in accordance with the Bond Ordinance.  As of 
October 1, 2024, there were no Senior Lien Util ities Services Tax Obligations outstanding under 
the Bond Ordinance.  For additional information relating to Senior Lien Utilities Services Tax 
Obligations, see "OUTSTANDING WATER RECLAMATION SYSTEM OBLIGATIONS – 
Senior Lien Utilities Services Tax Obligations" herein. 
"Pledged Utilities Services Tax"  is defined in the Bond Ordinance as the proceeds of the 
Utilities Services Tax available to make paym ents under the Bond Ordi nance after satisfying 
funding obligations with respect to Senior Lien Utilities Services Tax Obligations. 
"Utilities Services Tax" is defined in the Bond Ordinance as the taxes imposed, levied, and 
collected by the City pursuant to Section 166.231, Florida Statutes, and other applicable provisions 
of law on the purchase of electricity, metered natural gas, liquefied petroleum gas either metered 
or bottled, manufactured gas either metered or bottled, and water service and services competitive 
with those enumerated, as from time to time defined by ordina nce of the City.  For additional 
information relating to the Util ities Services Tax, including th e amounts imposed and levied by 
the City and historical collections , see "WATER RECLAMATION SYSTEM 
REVENUES – Utilities Services Tax" herein. 
"Senior Lien Utilities Servi ces Tax Obligations" is define d in the Bond Ordinance as 
obligations of the City incurr ed in accordance with the Bond Or dinance that are secured by a 
pledge of and lien on the Utilities Services Tax th at is senior and superior  to the pledge thereof 
and lien thereon granted pursuant to the Bond Ordinance. 
Whenever by reason of the insufficiency of Gross Revenues, the City is not able to fund 
the Costs of Operation and Maintenance or to ma ke deposits required to be  made into the Bond 
Service Fund or the Reserve Fund, the City is requi red to deposit Utilities Services Tax revenues 
available after satisfying current funding requiremen ts with respect to any Senior Lien Utilities 
Services Tax Obligations in an amount necessary to  cure such deficiencies to the credit of the 
Revenue Fund and apply such amounts in the priority described in the Bond Ordinance.  Pledged 
Utilities Services Tax proceeds not required in any month to cure deficiencies as described in the 
Bond Ordinance may be applied by the City for any lawful purpose.  See "SECURITY AND 
SOURCES OF PAYMENT FOR THE SERIES 2024 BONDS – Flow of Funds" below. 
The City reserves the right to incur obligations that may be secured by a lien on and pledge 
of the Utilities Service Tax that  is prior and superior to the pledge of and lien on the Pledged 
Utilities Services Tax under the Bond Ordinance so long as, at the time of issuance of any such  
12 
Senior Lien Utilities Services Tax Obligations, the amount of the Utilities Services Tax collected 
in any 12 consecutive months of the preceding 30 months is not less than 1.50 times the maximum 
annual debt service on the Senior Lien Utilities  Services Tax Obligati ons to be outstanding 
following the issuance of the Senior Lien Utilities Services Tax Obligations proposed to be issued, 
calculated in a manner substantially consistent with the methodology, assumptions and permitted 
adjustments provided in the Bond Ordinance with respect to the issuance of Additional Parity 
Obligations.  See "SECURITY AND SOUR CES OF PAYMENT FOR THE SERIES 2024 
BONDS – Flow of Funds" and "APPENDIX B – THE BOND ORDINANCE" attached hereto. 
The City has covenanted in the Bond Ordinance that so long as any principal of or interest 
on any of the Bonds are Outstanding, it will continue to levy and collect the Utilities Services Tax 
at the rate levied on the date of enactment of the Master Bond Ordinance and will not repeal, 
amend or modify the ordinance of the City levying the Utilities Services Tax in any manner so as 
to impair or adversely affect the power and obliga tion of the City to levy and collect the Utilities 
Services Tax in any manne r, the pledge of the Pledged Utilit ies Services Tax made in the Bond 
Ordinance, or the rights of the Bondholders. 
See "APPENDIX B – THE BOND ORDINANCE" attached hereto. 
Composite Reserve Account; Reserve Requirement for the Series 2024 Bonds 
The Reserve Requirement for the Series  2024 Bonds is the Composite Reserve 
Requirement.  The Series 2024 Bonds, together w ith any Additional Parity Obligations hereafter 
issued by the City and designated to be secu red by the Composite Reserve Account, will be 
additionally secured by the Composite Reserve Account in the Reserve Fund.  The "Composite 
Reserve Requirement" is defined in the Bond Ordinance as an amount of money, or the aggregate 
available amount under one or more Reserve Products, or a combination thereof, equal to the least 
of (a) the Maximum Bond Service Requirement calcu lated with respect to all Series of Bonds 
Outstanding under the Bond Ordina nce that are secured by the Composite Reserve Account, 
(b) 125% of the average annual Bond Service Requirement calculated with respect to all Series of 
Bonds Outstanding under the Bond Ordinance that are secured by the Composite Reserve Account, 
or (c) 10% of the aggregate stat ed original principal amount of all Series of Bonds Outstanding 
under the Bond Ordinance that are secured by the Composite Reserve Account, provided, however, 
that in determining the aggreg ate stated original principal amount of Bonds Outstanding for 
purposes of clause (c), the issue price of Bonds (net of pre-issu ance accrued interest) shall be 
substituted for the original stated principal amount of those Bonds if such Bonds were sold at either 
an original issue discount or premium exceedi ng two percent of the stat ed redemption price at 
maturity.  See "APPENDIX B – THE BOND ORDINANCE" attached hereto. 
Upon the issuance of the Series 2024 Bonds  and the refunding and redemption of the 
Refunded Bonds, the Series 2024 Bonds will be th e only Additional Parity Obligations under the 
Bond Ordinance.  Therefore, the Composite Reserve Requirement will initially be $9,753,500.00, 
of which $7,112,250.00 and $2,641,250.00 will be allocable to the Series 2024A Bonds and the 
Series 2024B Bonds, respectively.  See "E STIMATED SOURCES A ND USES OF FUNDS" 
herein.  
13 
Revenue Fund; Disposition of Revenues 
Under the terms of the Bond Or dinance, all Gross Revenues  of the Water Reclamation 
System and any amounts received by the City as direct subsidy, rebate or tax credit payments with 
respect to Bonds issued as Direct Subsidy Ob ligations, are required to be deposited into the 
Revenue Fund and transferred monthly on or before the 25th day of each month from the Revenue 
Fund in the following manner and order of priority: 
(a) The City shall first set as ide to pay or apply the amount necessary to pay the Costs 
of Operation and Maintenance for such month. 
(b) The Issuer shall next deposit into the Bond Service Fund and credit to the following 
accounts, in the following order (e xcept that payments into the Interest Account and the Parity 
Contract Obligations Account sha ll be on parity with each othe r, and the payments into the 
Principal Account and the Redemption Account shall be on a parity with each other), the following 
identified sums: 
(i) Interest Account: Taking into account actual and anticipated earnings in the 
Interest Account of the Bond Service Fund within the current Bond Year, such sum as will 
be sufficient to pay 1/6th of all interest coming due on all Outstanding Bonds, on the next 
interest payment date; provided, however, that  monthly deposits of interest, or portions 
thereof, shall not be required to be made to  the extent that mone y on deposit within such 
Interest Account is sufficient fo r such purpose.  In the event the City has issued Variable 
Rate Bonds, Commercial Paper Obligations, or  other types of Bonds pursuant to the 
provisions of the Bond Ordinanc e that bear interest payabl e other than on a semi-annual 
basis, Pledged Revenues shall be deposited at such other or additional times and amounts 
as necessary to pay any interest coming due on such Variable Rate Bonds, Commercial 
Paper Obligations, or other types of Bonds on the next interest paym ent date, all in the 
manner provided pursuant to a Supplemental Ordinance or Resolution of the City.  Any 
monthly payment out of Pledged Revenues to be deposited as set forth above, for the 
purpose of meeting interest payments for an y Series of Bonds, shall be adjusted, as 
appropriate, to reflect the frequen cy of interest payment dates applicable to such Series.  
Moneys in the Interest Account may be used only for the purposes  set forth in this 
paragraph (i).  Deposits to the Interest Account shall be increased or decreased each month 
to the extent required to timel y pay interest next coming due after making allowances for 
any accrued and capitalized interest and to make up any deficiency or loss that may 
otherwise arise. 
(ii) Parity Contract Obligations A ccount: Taking into acc ount the actual and 
anticipated earnings in the Parity Contract Obligations Account in the Bond Service Fund 
within the current Bond Year, a pro rata estimated amount necessary to build up over time 
the amount of any Parity Contract Obligati on which will next be due and payable or 
reasonably expected to be due and payable under any Qualified Agreement on the next 
payment date thereunder; provided, however, that the monthly amount to be so deposited 
may be adjusted, as appropriate, to reflect the frequency of payment dates thereunder (e.g., 
if such Parity Contract Obligations are required to be paid semi-annually, the City shall be 
required to deposit monthly an amount which is estimated to equal 1/6th of the next such  
14 
payment).  Moneys in the Parity Contract Obligations Account may be used only for the 
purposes set forth in this para graph (ii).  Deposits to the Parity Contract Obligations 
Account shall be increased or decreased each month to the extent required to timely pay 
Parity Contract Obligations next becoming due and payable and to make up any deficiency 
or loss that may otherwise arise. 
(iii)  Principal Account:  Taking into a ccount actual and anticipated earnings in 
the Principal Account of the Bond Service Fund within the current Bond Year, such sum 
as will be sufficient to pay 1/12th of the principal amount of the Outstanding Bonds which 
will mature and become due on such annual ma turity dates beginning the month which is 
12 months prior to the first principal matu rity date; provided, how ever, that monthly 
deposits for principal, or portions thereof, are not required to be made to the extent that 
money on deposit within such Principal Accoun t is sufficient for such purpose.  Any 
monthly payment out of Pledged Revenues to be deposited in the Principal Account for the 
purpose of meeting principal pa yments for any Series of B onds, shall be adjusted, as 
appropriate, to reflect the frequency of principal payment dates applicable to such Series.  
Deposits to the Principal Account shall be increased or decreased each month to the extent 
required to timely pay principal next beco ming due and payable and to make up any 
deficiency or loss that may otherwise arise. 
(iv)  Redemption Account: Such sum as will be sufficient to pay 1/12th of any 
Amortization Installment established for the mandatory redemption of Outstanding Bonds 
on such annual maturity date beginning the month which is 12 months prior to the first 
Amortization Installment date; provided, ho wever, that monthly deposits into the 
Redemption Account, or portions thereof, shall not be required to be made to the extent 
that money on deposit in the Redemption Account  is sufficient for such purpose.  The 
moneys in the Redemption Account shall be used solely for the purchase or redemption of 
the Term Bonds payable therefrom.  Deposits to the Redemption Account shall be 
increased or decreased each month to the extent required to tim ely pay Amortization 
Installments next becoming due and payable and to make up any deficiency or loss that 
may otherwise arise.  The City may at any time purchase any of said Term Bonds at prices 
not greater than the then redemption price of said Term Bonds.  If the Term Bonds are not 
then redeemable prior to matu rity, the City may purchase said  Term Bonds at prices not 
greater than the redemption price of such Term Bonds on the next ensuing redemption date.  
If Term Bonds are so purchased by the Cit y, the City will credit the account of such 
purchased Term Bonds against any current Amortization Installment to be paid by the City.  
If the City shall purchase or call for redemption in any year Term Bonds in excess of the 
Amortization Installment requ irement for such year, such excess of Term Bonds so 
purchased or redeemed shall be credited in such manner and at such times as the City shall 
determine. 
(c) To the extent that the amounts on depos it in the accounts of the Reserve Fund are 
less than the applicable Reserve Requirement, the City will next make deposits into the Reserve 
Fund from moneys remaining in the Revenue Fund, amounts which, after taking into account other 
funds then on deposit therein, will be sufficient to make the f unds on deposit therein equal to the 
Reserve Requirement for such account; provided, how ever, that if the funds  on deposit in the 
Reserve Fund are less than the Reserve Requirement as a result of a withdrawal therefrom to pay  
15 
debt service on the Bonds secured thereby, the am ount of such deficiency may be restored in 
substantially equal monthly payments over a pe riod ending not later than 12 months after the 
month in which the withdrawal causing such deficiency occurred.  If there are not sufficient funds 
in the Revenue Fund available to make the required deposit to the accounts in the Reserve Fund, 
the amount available shall be deposited to the va rious accounts pro rata, based upon the relative 
Reserve Requirements for each account. 
Notwithstanding anything in the Bond Ordinance to the contrary, the City shall not be 
required to fully fund an account in the Reserve Fund at the time of issuance of any Series of Bonds 
under the Bond Ordinance if it provides on the date of issuance of such Series of Bonds in lieu of 
such funds, a Reserve Product, in an amount equal to the differen ce between the Reserve 
Requirement and the sums then on deposit in the applicable account of the Reserve Fund; provided, 
however, that in no event shall the use of such Reserve Product be permitted if it would cause any 
existing rating on the Bonds or any Series thereo f to be lowered, suspen ded, or withdrawn.  If a 
disbursement is made from a Reserve Product to fund a deficiency in amounts available to pay 
debt service on the applicable Series of Bonds, the City shall be obligated to reinstate the maximum 
limits of such Reserve Product immediately upon such disbursement or to replace such Reserve 
Product by depositing into the applicable accoun t of the Reserve Fund from the first Pledged 
Revenues available for deposit into the Reserv e Fund, funds in the maximum amount payable 
under such Reserve Product prior to such disbursement, plus amounts necessary to reimburse the 
provider thereof for previous disbursements made under such Reserve Product, or a combination 
of such alternatives, and for purposes of this paragraph, amounts necessary to satisfy such 
reimbursement obligation and other obligations to the provider of such Reserve Product shall be 
deemed required payments into the applicable a ccount of the Reserve Fund, but shall be used by 
the City to satisfy its obligations to such provider. 
Notwithstanding the foregoing, if one or more  accounts in the Reserve Fund have been 
funded with cash or Permitted Investments, the City may, at any time in its discretion, substitute a 
Reserve Product, for all or a portion of the cash and Permitted Investments in any such account, 
and the City may then withdraw such cash and Permitted Investments from such account and apply 
them to any lawful purpose of the Water Reclam ation System, so long as  (a) the same does not 
adversely affect any credit rating then in effect with respect to the applicable Series of Outstanding 
Bonds and (b) the City obtains an opinion of Co -Bond Counsel that such actions will not, in and 
of themselves, adversely affect the exclusion from gross income of interest for the applicable 
Series of Bonds (if other than Taxable Bonds) for federal income tax purposes and will not cause 
any Bonds secured by such account that constitute Direct Subsidy Obligations to cease to qualify 
as such. 
Cash on deposit in the applicab le account of the Reserve Fund is required to be used (or 
investments purchased with such cash shall be li quidated and the proceeds  applied as required) 
prior to drawing on any Reserve Product.  If more  than one Reserve Product is deposited in an 
account of the Reserve Fund, drawi ngs thereon and repayment of co sts associated therewith will 
be made on a pro rata basis, calculated by reference to the maximum amounts available thereunder. 
Moneys in the accounts of the Reserve F und may be used only for the purpose of the 
payment of Amortization Installments, principal of, or interest on the Outstanding Bonds secured  
16 
thereby when the other moneys allocated to th e Bond Service Fund are in sufficient therefor, and 
for no other purpose. 
Permitted Investments on deposit in the Reserve Fund are required to be valued at fair 
value pursuant to generally accepted accounting princi ples at least annually.  In the event of the 
refunding of any Series of Bonds, the City ma y withdraw from the account of the Reserve Fund 
securing such Series, all or any portion of the amounts accumulated therei n with respect to the 
Bonds being refunded and deposit  such amounts as required by the ordinance or resolution 
authorizing the refunding of such Series of B onds; provided that such w ithdrawal shall not be 
made unless (a) immediately ther eafter, the Bonds being refunded sh all be deemed to have been 
paid pursuant to the Bond Ordinance, and (b) the amount remaining in such account of the Reserve 
Fund after giving effect to  the issuance of such refunding ob ligations and the disposition of the 
proceeds thereof are not less than the Reserve Requirement for any Bonds then Outstanding which 
are secured thereby. 
(d)  From the moneys remaining in the Re venue Fund, the City will next deposit into 
the Subordinated Debt Service Fund an amount requi red to be paid as pr ovided in the ordinance 
or resolution or agreement of the City authorizing such Subordinated Debt.  See "OUTSTANDING 
WATER RECLAMATION SYSTEM OBLIGATIONS - Subordinated Debt" herein. 
(e)  The City will next apply and deposit monthly from the moneys remaining on 
deposit in the Revenue Fund into the Renewal, Replacement and Improvement Fund, an amount 
at least equal to 1/12th of five percent of th e Gross Revenues received  during the immediately 
preceding Fiscal Year, plus an amount equal to any unrestored wit hdrawal made to pay Costs of 
Operation and Maintenance or to cure a defici ency in the Bond Servic e Fund as contemplated 
below, until the amounts on deposit therein are e qual to three and one-half percent of the 
depreciated value of the deprecia ble assets of the Water Reclam ation System for the preceding 
Fiscal Year; provided, however, that no further deposits shall be required whenever and so long as 
there is then on deposit in the Renewal, Replacement and Improvement Fund not less than 
$1,500,000 or such lesser amount as shall be recommended by a Qualified Independent Consultant 
as complying with Prudent Utility Standards.  The moneys in the Renewal, Replacement and 
Improvement Fund shall be used only for the purpose of paying the cost of extraordinary repairs, 
extensions, enlargements or additions to, or the replacement of capital assets of the Water 
Reclamation System or emergency repairs thereto.  Funds on ha nd in the Renewal, Replacement 
and Improvement Fund may be used to pay curre nt Costs of Operation and Maintenance to the 
extent moneys on deposit in the Revenue Fund are insufficient for such purposes.  The moneys on 
deposit in such fund may also be used to supplement the Bond Service Fund, if necessary, in order 
to prevent a default in the payment of the principal and interest on the Bonds. 
(f) The balance of any moneys remaining in the Revenue Fund after making the above 
required payments will be deposited into the Surplus Fund and may be used for any lawful purpose, 
including any deposit to the Rate Stabilization Fund that the City deems appropriate; provided, 
however, that none of such moneys shall be used for any purposes other than those specified above 
unless all current payments, including any deficiencies for prior payments, have been made in full 
and unless the City shall have complied fully with  all the covenants and provisions of the Bond 
Ordinance.

Rate Stabilization Fund 
The City may transfer into the Rate Stabilization Fund such moneys which are on deposit 
in the Surplus Fund as it deems appropriate.  The City may transfer such amount of moneys from 
the Rate Stabilization Fund to the Revenue Fund as it deems appropriate; provided, however, that 
on or prior to each principal and interest payment date for the Bonds (in no event earlier than the 
25th day of the month next preceding such payment date), moneys in the Rate Stabilization Fund 
shall be applied for the payment into the Interest Account, the Parity Contract Obligation Account, 
the Principal Account and the Re demption Account when the moneys  therein are insufficient to 
pay the principal of and interest on the Bonds coming due and to pay any Parity Contract 
Obligations.  So long as all current payments, including any deficiencies for prior payments, shall 
have been made in full and the City shall not be in default of any of the covenants and provisions 
of the Bond Ordinance, the City may withdraw amounts on deposit in the Rate Stabilization Fund 
to be applied for any lawful purpose of the City. 
Moneys transferred from the Rate Stabilization Fund and deposited into the Revenue Fund 
in accordance with the terms of the Bond Ordina nce are part of Gross Revenues under the Bond 
Ordinance.  Moneys transferred from the Rate Stabilization Fund into the Revenue Fund within 
90 days following the end of a Fiscal Year may be designated by the City as Gross Revenues of 
such prior Fiscal Year.

Additional Parity Obligations 
"Additional Parity Obligations" is defined in  the Master Bond Ordinance as additional 
obligations issued or incurred in compliance with  the terms, conditions and limitations contained 
in the Bond Ordinance and which (a) shall have a lien on the Pledged Revenues equal to that of 
the Outstanding Bonds and any Parity Contract Obligations, (b) shall be payable from the Pledged 
Revenues on a parity with the Outstanding Bonds and any Parity Contract Obligations, and 
(c) except as expressly provided in the Master Bond Ordinance or in a Supplemental Ordinance or 
Resolution, shall rank equally in all other respec ts with the Outstanding Bonds and any Parity 
Contract Obligations. 
No Additional Parity Obligations may be i ssued under the Bond Ordinance, except upon 
the conditions and in the manner set forth below: 
(a) The Chief Financial Officer shall file a certificate stating that: (i) they have 
reviewed the books and records of  the City relative to the Water  Reclamation System and the 
Pledged Revenues; and (ii) the amount of th e Pledged Revenues deri ved for any consecutive 
12 months out of the 30 months preceding the date of issuance of the proposed Additional Parity 
Obligations (the "Test Period") adjusted as provided in paragraphs (b), (c), (d), (e) and/or (f) below, 
is not less than 125% of the Maximum Bond Se rvice Requirement becoming due in any Bond 
Year thereafter on (A) all Bonds issued under th e Bond Ordinance that will remain Outstanding 
upon the issuance of such Additional Parity Ob ligations and (B) on the Additional Parity 
Obligations proposed to be issued. 
(b) Upon recommendation of the Qualified Independent Consultants, the Pledged 
Revenues certified pursuant to (a)(ii) above may be adjusted for purposes of issuing Additional 
Parity Obligations by including: (i) 100% of the additional Net Revenues which in the opinion of 
the Qualified Independent Consultant would have been derived by the City from rate increases 
adopted before the Additional Parity Obligations ar e issued, if such rate increases had been in 
effect during the Test Period, and (ii) 100% of the additiona l Net Revenues estimated by the 
Qualified Independent Consultant to be derived during the first full 12 month period after the 
facilities of the Water Reclamation System are extended, enlarged, improved or added to with the 
proceeds of the Additional Parity Obligations proposed to be issued. 
(c) Upon recommendation of the Qualified Independent Consultants, if the Additional 
Parity Obligations are to be issued for the pur pose of acquiring an existing wastewater system 
and/or any other utilit y system in accordance with the Bond Ordinance, the Pledged Revenues  
20 
certified pursuant to (a)(ii) above may be adjusted by including 100% of the additional estimated 
Net Revenues which in the written opinion of the Qualified Independent Consultants will be 
derived from the acquired facilities during the first full 12-month period after the issuance of such 
Additional Parity Obligations (the Qualified Independent Consultants' report shall be based on the 
actual operating revenues of  the acquired utility for a recent 12-month period adjusted to reflect 
the City's ownership and the City's rate structure in effect with respect to the Water Reclamation 
System at the time of the issuance of the Additional Parity Obligations). 
(d) Upon recommendation of the Qualified Inde pendent Consultants, if the number of 
connections as of the first day of the month in which the proposed Additional Parity Obligations 
are to be issued exceeds the average number of such connections during such 12 consecutive month 
period, then the Pledged Revenues certified pursuant to (a)(ii) above may be adjusted to include 
the Net Revenues which would have been receive d in such 12 consecuti ve months if those 
additional connections had also been connected to the Water Reclamation System during all of 
such 12 consecutive months. 
(e) Upon recommendation of the Qualified I ndependent Consultant, if the City has 
entered into a contract for a duration of not less than the final maturity of the proposed Additional 
Parity Obligations, with any public body, whereby the City has agreed  to furnish services for the 
collection, treatment or disposal of  sewage or agreed to furnish services in connection with any 
water system or any other utility  system, then the Pledged Revenues certified pursuant to (a)(ii) 
above may be increased (to the extent such amounts were not reflected in such Net Revenues) by 
the minimum amount which the p ublic body shall guarantee to pa y in any one year for the 
furnishing of services by the City, after deduct ing from such payment the estimated Cost of 
Operation and Maintenance attributable in such year to such services. 
(f) Upon recommendations of the Qualified In dependent Consultants, if there is an 
estimated increase in Net Revenues to be received by the City as a result of additions, extensions 
or improvements to the Water Reclamation System during the period of three years following the 
completion of such additions, extensions or improvements financed with the proceeds of Bonds or 
Additional Parity Obligations, then the Pledge d Revenues derived from the Water Reclamation 
System certified pursuant to (a)(ii) above ma y be increased by 50% of the average annual 
additional Net Revenues calculated for such three year period. 
(g) The City does not need to comply with the provisions of (a) above if and to the 
extent the Additional Parity Obligations to be issued are refunding bonds and the City delivers a 
certificate of the Chief Financial Officer se tting forth the Maximum Annual Debt Service 
Requirement (i) for the Bonds then Outstanding and (ii) for all Series of Bonds to be Outstanding 
immediately thereafter and stating that the Maximum Annual Debt Service Requirement pursuant 
to (g)(ii) above is not greater than that set forth pursuant to (g)(i) above. 
(h) The City does not need to comply with the provisions of (a) above if and to the 
extent the Bonds to be issued are for the pur pose of providing any necessary additional funds 
required for completion of any improvements to the Water Reclamation System ("Completion 
Bonds") if originally financed with the proceeds of Bonds; provided that such Completion Bonds 
may not exceed 10% of th e total principal amount  of Bonds estimated to  be required for such  
21 
improvements to the Water Reclamation System at the time of issuance of the initial Series of 
Bonds to finance such improvements. 
(i) The Chief Financial Officer certifies that the City is not in default in carrying out 
its obligations under the Bond Ordinance and no Event of Default has occurred and is continuing 
under the Bond Ordinance, and all payments requi red to be made into the funds and accounts 
established under the Bond Ordinance have been made. 
(j) The Supplemental Ordinance or Reso lution authorizing th e issuance of the 
Additional Parity Obligations shall recite that all of the covenants contained in the Bond Ordinance 
will be applicable to such Additional Parity Obligations. 
(k) Notwithstanding anything to the Bond Or dinance to the cont rary, no Additional 
Parity Obligations may be issued if an Event of Default would continue beyond such issuance. 
Rate Covenant 
Pursuant to the Bond Ordinance, the City covenanted as follows: 
(a) The City will fix, establish, revise from time to time whenever necessary, maintain 
and collect always such fees, rates, rentals and other charges for the use of the products, services 
and facilities of the Water Reclamation System which will always provide, Pledged Revenues in 
each Fiscal Year sufficient to pay 125% of the Bond Service Requirement on all Outstanding 
Bonds in the applicable Bond Year.  
(b) Pledged Revenues in each Fiscal  Year will also be suff icient to provide 100% of 
the Bond Service Requirement on all Outstanding Bonds in the applicable Bond Year, any amounts 
required by the terms of the Bond Ordinance to be deposited into the Reserve Fund, the Renewal, 
Replacement and Improvement Fund and debt serv ice on other obligations payable from the Net 
Revenues of the Water Reclamation System, a nd other payments, and all allocations and 
applications of revenues required by the Bond Ordinance in such Fiscal Year. 
(c) Net Revenues will not be reduced so as to  render them insufficient to provide 
revenues for the purposes provided by the Bond Ordinance. 
Limited Obligation 
The Series 2024 Bonds do not constitute a gene ral obligation or indebtedness of the City 
within the meaning of any constitutional, statutory or charter provisions or limitations, but will be 
payable solely from and secured by a lien upon and a pledge of the Pledged Revenues in the manner 
and to the extent provided in the Bond Ordinanc e.  No Holder of Series 2024 Bonds shall ever 
have the right to compel the exercise of the ad valorem taxing power of the City or taxation in any 
form on any real or personal property, or to compel the City to pay such principal and interest on 
the Series 2024 Bonds from any other funds of the City.  The Series 2024 Bonds shall not constitute 
a lien upon the Water Reclamation System, or any part  thereof, or on any other property of or in 
the City, but shall constitute a lien only on the Pledged Revenues in the manner and to the extent 
provided in the Bond Ordinance.  See "APPE NDIX B – THE BOND ORDINANCE" attached 
hereto.

Subordinated Debt 
Outstanding Subordinated Debt .  As of October 1, 2024, the hereinafter defined 
Outstanding CWSRF Program Loans were the only Subordinated Debt outstanding under the Bond 
Ordinance.  Subordinated Debt is payable from Pledged Revenues on a junior, inferior, and 
subordinate basis to Additional Parity Obligations. 
The State of Florida Clean Water State Revolving Fund Program (the "CWSRF Program") 
provides low-interest loans to local governments for planning, de signing, and constructing water 
pollution control facilities under Chapter 62-503, F.A.C.  As of September 30, 2023, the City had 
14 loans payable to the State under the CWSRF Pr ogram in the aggregate principal amount of 
$75,601,704 (the "Outstanding CWSRF Program Loans").  In addition, the City has been awarded 
an additional loan under the CWSRF Program in the principal amount of $58,000,000.  However, 
the City has not made any draws on such loan.  The applicable interest rate on the Outstanding 
CWSRF Program Loans range from 0.40% to 2.66%.

THE CITY 
The City operates under a mayor-council form of government.  The Mayor is the City's 
Chief Executive Officer, elected for a term of four years.  In addition to serving as presiding officer 
and as a voting member of the City Council, the Mayor's responsibilities include the enforcement 
of laws, control of City departments and divi sions, appointment and re moval of officers and 
employees, supervision of City  property and negotiations of contracts.  The Mayor makes 
recommendations for creation of ordinances and resoluti ons to the City Counc il and presents the 
annual budget for approval. 
The City Council is the legislative branch of City government a nd is responsible for 
taxation, finances, zoning regulation and boundaries.  The City Council (consisting of, the Mayor 
elected at large as Chairman a nd six district commissioners) reviews plans and specifications for 
public improvements, enacts legislation governing City operations and approves the City budget.  
Commissioners are elected on a district-wide basis for four-year terms on a two-year staggered 
basis.  The Mayor and the members of the City Council are not subject to term limits. 
The Mayor is the Chief Executive Officer with ten departments reporting to him: Business 
& Financial Services; Economic Development; Families, Parks and Recreation; Fire; Housing and 
Community Development; Human Resources; Orlando Venues; Police; Transportation; and Public 
Works.  The Mayor is assisted in the day-to -day oversight of City  operations by the Chief 
Administrative Officer, Chief Financial Officer and City Attorney.  Separately, under the Mayor's 
Chief of Staff, there are seven programmati c areas: the City Clerk; Communications and 
Neighborhood Relations; Community Affairs; C onstituent Relations; Governmental Relations; 
Human Relations; and Multicultural Affairs. 
Additional information relating to the City is available on EMMA. 
MANAGEMENT AND EMPLOYEES OF THE WATER RECLAMATION SYSTEM 
Management 
The following are brief resumes of the City's Mayor and certa in appointed officials, and 
key personnel involved in the administration and operation of the City and/or the Water 
Reclamation System. 
Mayor Buddy Dyer is a native of Central Florida, born in Orlando and raised in the nearby 
City of Kissimmee.  Following graduation from high school, he was awarded a scholarship to 
Brown University where his studi es were concentrated on civil engineering.  Upon graduation, 
Mayor Dyer returned to Orlando to work as an environmental engineer, later enrolling in the 
University of Florida Law School, where he was named editor-in-chief of the University of Florida 
Law Review.  Following graduation from law school, Mayor Dyer began his legal career with the 
Orlando law firm of Winderweedle, Haines, Ward & Woodman.  Prior to becoming Mayor, Buddy 
Dyer served the Orlando area for ten years as a St ate Senator in the Florida Legislature.  Mayor 
Dyer was first elected in 2003 to fill an unexpired term and was subs equently re-elected to full 
four-year terms in each election since 2004.

Employees 
The Water Reclamation Division has 280  full-time positions budge ted for Fiscal Year 
2025.  The Florida Department of Environmental Protection ("FDEP ") specifically requires that 
certain types of plants have ce rtified wastewater treatment plan t operators on duty twenty-four 
hours a day, seven days a week.  The City is in full compliance with this requirement.  Currently, 
most of the Water Reclamation Division's job positions are covered by a collective bargaining 
agreement either between the City and the Laborers International Union of North America, Local 
#678 or between the City and the Service Employees International Union, Local #8.  The current 
collective bargaining agreements expire on September 30, 2025.  Th e City currently expects to 
begin discussions with the unions before the end of 2024.  The Water R eclamation Division has 
never been subject to a strike by its public empl oyees and its contracts with the unions prohibit 
strikes, slowdowns, or other work  stoppages.  In addition, Florida Statutes specifically prohibit 
strikes by public employees.  Th e City has a full-time professi onal labor relations staff and 
characterizes its relationship with the Water Reclamation System's employees as good. 
THE WATER RECLAMATION SYSTEM 
General 
References to the "Water Reclamation Syst em" herein shall have the same meaning 
assigned to the term "System" in the B ond Ordinance.  See "APPENDIX B – THE BOND 
ORDINANCE" attached hereto. 
The Water Reclamation System is operated by the Water Reclamation Division within the 
City's Department of Public Works.  The Water  Reclamation System is an integrated system 
comprised of: (a) a collection system to collect and transmit wastewater from customers to the 
water reclamation facilities for treatment; (b ) three water reclamation facilities ("WRFs"), 
including (i) the Iron Bridge Regi onal WRF (the "Iron Bridge Plan t"), (ii) the Water Conserv I 
WRF (the "Conserv I Plant"), and (iii) the Water Conserv II WRF (the "Conserv II Plant"), which 
treat the incoming wastewater to a point where it is safe to be reused in the community for irrigation 
and other beneficial purposes; and (c) a reclaimed water distribution system to convey the treated 
water to irrigation customers to use in lieu of drinking water, to rapid infiltration basins for aquifer 
recharge or to environmental enhancement projects such as man-made wetlands systems.  
Together, these components provide a comprehensive means of collecting, treating, and 
beneficially reusing wastewater for the City.  The collection syst em referenced in (a) above and 
certain related facilities, including the Iron Bridge Plant, the Conserv I Plan t, and the Conserv II  
28 
Plant are referred to herein as the "Wastewater System."  The reclaimed water distribution system 
referenced in (c) above and certain related facilities, including the Iron Bridge Plant, the Conserv I 
Plant, and the Conserv II Plant are referred to herein as the "Reclaimed Water System."   
The Water Reclamation System currently prov ides treatment capacity  to the City and a 
number of other jurisdictions (portions of unincorporated Or ange County, Florida ("Orange 
County") and Seminole County, Florida ("Seminol e County"), and the Cities of Casselberry, 
Maitland and Winter Park, servicing approxima tely 312,000 residents.  The Water Reclamation 
System has historically been divided into the easterly and westerly subsystems.  The easterly 
subsystem is served by the Iron Bridge Plant, a 40 million gallons per day ("MGD") facility, and 
the Conserv I Plant, a 7.5 MGD facility.  The westerly subsystem is served by the Conserv II Plant, 
a 25 MGD facility.  The Water Reclamation System has the ability to transfer wastewater from the 
eastern part of the City to the western part of the City allowing the flexibility to equalize flows 
between the WRFs.  For maps of the hereinafter defined Wastewater System Service Area and the 
Reclaimed Water System Service Ar ea, see "THE WATER RECLAMATION 
SYSTEM – City/County Territorial Agreement" below. 
City/County Territorial Agreement 
On May 4, 1994, a Wastewater Service Territorial Agreement was entered into between 
the City and Orange County in order to define the City's wastewater service area (the "Territorial 
Agreement").  Pursuant to the Territorial Agreement, the City agreed to provide wastewater service 
to all incorporated and unincor porated properties within its territorial area, which currently 
encompasses the areas depicted in  the map entitled "City of Orlando Wast ewater Service Areas" 
below (the "Wastewater System Service Area") .  To facilitate connection to the Wastewater 
System, the City established a septic tank ab andonment policy to allow for certain credits on 
wastewater connection and construction costs that are incurred by new customers originally served 
by septic systems in the Wastewater System Service Area, provided that these new customers are 
annexed into the City.  The costs of these cred its are divided between th e General Construction 
Fund under the Water Reclamation Fund and the City's General Fund.  Since the establishment of 
the credit program, several unincorporated neighborhood areas previously in Orange County have 
annexed into the City to take advantage of the reduced Wastewater System connection charges. 
Pursuant to another provision of the Territorial Agreement, Orange County has redirected 
its flows from the Conserv II Plan t to its own treatment facilit y, thereby freeing up 2.8 MGD of 
capacity at the Conserv II Plant for future City customers in the Conserv II Plant service area 
within the Wastewater System Service Area.  A connection remains to allow flows to be diverted 
back to the Wastewater System in the event Orange County experiences problems with its system 
or a pipeline failure. 
Within a few years of entering into the Territorial Agreement, the City and Orange County 
began constructing and expanding reclaimed water systems to provide reclaimed water irrigation 
service to their respective customers.  On March 4, 2004, the City and Orange County entered into 
an amendment to the Territorial Agreement establishing reclaimed water service territorial areas 
for the City and Orange County.  The City provides reclaimed water service in the areas depicted 
in the map entitled "City of Orlando Reclaimed Water Service Areas" below (the "Reclaimed 
Water System Service Area").  Establishing territorial areas allowed the City and Orange County  
29 
to plan the expansion of their respective recl aimed water systems as discussed further under the 
section entitled "THE WATER RECLAMATION SYSTEM – Reclaimed Water System" below. 
[REMAINDER OF PAGE INTENTIONALLY LEFT BLANK]

Wastewater System 
Wastewater System Service Area and Customers .  The Wastewater System Service Area 
spans an area of approximately 110 square miles.  With recent annexations, the City's incorporated 
area has expanded to approximately 138 square miles with areas outside the Wastewater System 
Service Area being typically served by Orange County Utilities.  The Wastewater System serves 
approximately 84,400 residential and commercial wastewater accounts and its customers include 
single-family residential,  multi-family residential, commercial properties,  industrial facilities, 
theme parks, government facilities, and schools. 
Transmission System.  The Wastewater System conveys wastewater to the three WRFs 
through its collection and transmission system.  There are approximately 15,625 manholes, 232 lift 
stations and over 852 miles of piping in the publicly maintained portion of the Wastewater System 
responsible for collecting and transmitting the wastewater for treatment.  
Interconnect Systems .  To the extent possible, the City has designed and developed 
interconnecting systems, which allow the Wastewater System to re direct flows from one plant to 
another and provide flexibility to equalize flows between the WRFs.  The City has the capability 
to redirect 4.0 MGD of wastewater flow both to and from the Conserv I Plant and the Iron Bridge 
Plant.  In addition, the City has developed an interconnect sy stem which allows 2.0 to 3.0 MGD 
of wastewater to be redirected between the Cons erv II Plant and the Iron Bridge Plant.  Finally, 
the City has the ability to redirect 0.75 MGD from the Conserv II Plant to Orange County's South 
Water Reclamation Facility on an emergency basis.

For additional information regarding the Conserv I Plant, the Conserv II Plant, and the Iron
